---
layout: "post"
title: "HoTT-Book Exercises"
date: "2018-04-08"
categories: type-theory
---

This is a self-contained version of some solutions for HoTT-Book's exercises.
The idea is to unpackage all as long as possible to get a better understanding.
Many changes can be appear running this experiment. The solutions are
type-checked as a whole using Agda v2.5.3.


## Requirements

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Agda pragma for consistency with HoTT:

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="521" class="Symbol">{-#</a> <a id="525" class="Keyword">OPTIONS</a> <a id="533" class="Option">--without-K</a> <a id="545" class="Symbol">#-}</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------


Equality type defintion also called Identity type:

## Chapter 1

### Exercise 1.1

<div class="exercise">
Given functions $$f : A \to B$$ and $$g:B\to C$$, define
their composite $$ g\circ f:A\to C$$.
</div>

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="_∘_" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%88%98_" class="Function Operator">_∘_</a> <a id="1994" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="1996" class="Symbol">∀</a> <a id="1998" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="1999" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#1999" class="Bound">i</a> <a id="2001" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#2001" class="Bound">j</a> <a id="2003" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#2003" class="Bound">k</a><a id="2004" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="2006" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="2007" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#2007" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="2009" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="2011" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="2015" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#1999" class="Bound">i</a><a id="2016" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="2018" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#2018" class="Bound">B</a> <a id="2020" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="2022" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="2026" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#2001" class="Bound">j</a><a id="2027" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="2029" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#2029" class="Bound">C</a> <a id="2031" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="2033" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="2037" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#2003" class="Bound">k</a><a id="2038" class="Symbol">}</a>
    <a id="2044" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="2046" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="2047" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#2018" class="Bound">B</a> <a id="2049" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="2051" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#2029" class="Bound">C</a><a id="2052" class="Symbol">)</a>
    <a id="2058" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="2060" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="2061" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#2007" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="2063" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="2065" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#2018" class="Bound">B</a><a id="2066" class="Symbol">)</a>
    <a id="2072" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="2074" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#2007" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="2076" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="2078" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#2029" class="Bound">C</a>
<a id="2080" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#2080" class="Bound">g</a> <a id="2082" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%88%98_" class="Function Operator">∘</a> <a id="2084" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#2084" class="Bound">f</a> <a id="2086" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="2088" class="Symbol">λ</a> <a id="2090" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#2090" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="2092" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="2094" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#2080" class="Bound">g</a> <a id="2096" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="2097" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#2084" class="Bound">f</a> <a id="2099" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#2090" class="Bound">x</a><a id="2100" class="Symbol">)</a>{% endraw %}</pre>
<div class="exercise">
Show that we have $$h \circ (g\circ f) \equiv (h\circ g)\circ f$$.
</div>
<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="∘-assoc" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%88%98-assoc" class="Function">∘-assoc</a> <a id="2231" class="Symbol">:</a> <a ### Exercise 1.2

<div class="exercise">
Derive the recursion principle for products $$\mathsf{rec}_{A\times B}$$
using only the projections, and verify that the definitional equalities
are valid. Do the same for $$\Sigma$$-types.
</div>

Let's add some machinery to handle levels of the universe needed for
the following exercises including this one:

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="2769" class="Keyword">open</a> <a id="2774" class="Keyword">import</a> <a id="2781" href="Agda.Primitive.html" class="Module">Agda.Primitive</a> <a id="2796" class="Keyword">public</a>
  <a id="2805" class="Keyword">using</a> <a id="2811" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="2812" href="Agda.Primitive.html#Level" class="Postulate">Level</a><a id="2817" class="Symbol">;</a> <a id="2819" href="Agda.Primitive.html#_%E2%8A%94_" class="Primitive Operator">_⊔_</a><a id="2822" class="Symbol">;</a> <a id="2824" href="Agda.Primitive.html#lzero" class="Primitive">lzero</a><a id="2829" class="Symbol">;</a> <a id="2831" href="Agda.Primitive.html#lsuc" class="Primitive">lsuc</a><a id="2835" class="Symbol">)</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

To solve this problem we need:

  - Σ-type definition

  - Product type definition

  - Review the recursion principle, what exactly it consists of.
    Maybe this refresh our minds (see Pp. 42 HoTT-Book).

    <p class="equation">
    $$ \mathsf{rec}_{\sum\limits_{(x : A) } B(x)}
      : \prod\limits_{(C : U)} (\Pi_{(x : A)} B(x) \rightarrow C) \rightarrow
        \sum_{(x : A)} B(x) \rightarrow C
    $$
    </p>

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Σ-type (sigma type) definition (see the definition without projections
[here](https://github.com/jonaprieto/hott-book/blob/master/other/prelim.agda#L20)):

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="3518" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="Σ-Def₁" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81" class="Module">Σ-Def₁</a> <a id="3532" class="Keyword">where</a>

  <a id="3541" class="Keyword">record</a> <a id="Σ-Def₁.Σ" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81.%CE%A3" class="Record">Σ</a> <a id="3550" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="3551" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#3551" class="Bound">a</a> <a id="3553" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#3553" class="Bound">b</a><a id="3554" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="3556" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="3557" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#3557" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="3559" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="3561" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="3565" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#3551" class="Bound">a</a><a id="3566" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="3568" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="3569" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#3569" class="Bound">B</a> <a id="3571" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="3573" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#3557" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="3575" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="3577" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="3581" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#3553" class="Bound">b</a><a id="3582" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="3584" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="3586" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="3590" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="3591" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#3551" class="Bound">a</a> <a id="3593" href="Agda.Primitive.html#_%E2%8A%94_" class="Primitive Operator">⊔</a> <a id="3595" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#3553" class="Bound">b</a><a id="3596" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="3598" class="Keyword">where</a>
    <a id="3608" class="Keyword">constructor</a> <a id="Σ-Def₁.Σ._,_" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81.%CE%A3._%2C_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">_,_</a>
    <a id="3628" class="Keyword">field</a>
      <a id="Σ-Def₁.Σ.proj₁" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81.%CE%A3.proj%E2%82%81" class="Field">proj₁</a> <a id="3646" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="3648" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#3557" class="Bound">A</a>
      <a id="Σ-Def₁.Σ.proj₂" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81.%CE%A3.proj%E2%82%82" class="Field">proj₂</a> <a id="3662" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="3664" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#3569" class="Bound">B</a> <a id="3666" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81.%CE%A3.proj%E2%82%81" class="Field">proj₁</a>

  <a id="3675" class="Keyword">open</a> <a id="3680" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3" class="Module">Σ</a> <a id="3682" class="Keyword">public</a>
<a id="3689" class="Comment">-- _,_ : (proj₁ : A) → B proj₁ → Σ A B.</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

Its recursor with a function $$g : \prod_{(x : A)} B(x)\rightarrow C$$
that we provide.

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="3843" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="Σ-Rec₁" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Rec%E2%82%81" class="Module">Σ-Rec₁</a> <a id="3857" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="3858" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#3858" class="Bound">i</a> <a id="3860" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#3860" class="Bound">j</a> <a id="3862" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#3862" class="Bound">k</a><a id="3863" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="3865" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#3865" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="3867" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="3869" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="3873" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#3858" class="Bound">i</a><a id="3874" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="3876" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#3876" class="Bound">B</a> <a id="3878" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="3880" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#3865" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="3882" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="3884" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="3888" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#3860" class="Bound">j</a><a id="3889" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="3891" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#3891" class="Bound">C</a> <a id="3893" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="3895" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="3899" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#3862" class="Bound">k</a><a id="3900" class="Symbol">}</a>
             <a id="3915" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="3916" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#3916" class="Bound">g</a> <a id="3918" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="3920" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="3921" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#3921" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="3923" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="3925" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#3865" class="Bound">A</a><a id="3926" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="3928" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="3930" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#3876" class="Bound">B</a> <a id="3932" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#3921" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="3934" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="3936" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#3891" class="Bound">C</a><a id="3937" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="3939" class="Keyword">where</a>

  <a id="3948" class="Keyword">open</a> <a id="3953" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81" class="Module">Σ-Def₁</a> <a id="3960" class="Keyword">using</a> <a id="3966" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="3967" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81.%CE%A3" class="Record">Σ</a> <a id="3969" class="Symbol">;</a> <a id="3971" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81.%CE%A3.proj%E2%82%81" class="Field">proj₁</a><a id="3976" class="Symbol">;</a> <a id="3978" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81.%CE%A3.proj%E2%82%82" class="Field">proj₂</a><a id="3983" class="Symbol">;</a> <a id="3985" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81.%CE%A3._%2C_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">_,_</a> <a id="3989" class="Symbol">)</a>

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

On the other hand, the product type is just a particular case of the sigma type
when the codomain is not dependent, as we can see next by omitting the argument
in `(λ _ → B)`.

Its recursor with a function $$g : A \rightarrow B \rightarrow C$$ that we provide.

### Exercise 1.3

<p class="exercise">
Derive the induction principle for products $$\mathsf{ind}_{A\times B}$$,
using only the projections and the propositional uniqueness principle
$$\mathsf{uniq}_{A\times B}$$.
Verify that the definitional equalities are valid.
</p>

To solve this problem, recall the uniqueness principle (Pp. 29. HoTT-Book)

- The **propositional uniqueness principle** says that
every element of $$A\times B$$ is equal to a pair.

<p class="equation">
  $$ \mathsf{uniq}_{A\times B}
     : \prod_{(x : A \times B)} ((\mathsf{proj}_{1}(x) , \mathsf{proj}_{2}(x))
       \equiv_{A\times B} x).
  $$
</p>

Product type definition using `data`:

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="5561" class="Comment">-- this would be trivial in agda due to definitional η for records</a>
<a id="5628" class="Comment">-- so Capriotti defined a product type without η:</a>
<a id="5678" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="×-Def₂" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82" class="Module">×-Def₂</a> <a id="5692" class="Keyword">where</a>

  <a id="5701" class="Keyword">data</a> <a id="×-Def₂._×_" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82._%C3%97_" class="Datatype Operator">_×_</a> <a id="5710" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="5711" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#5711" class="Bound">i</a> <a id="5713" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#5713" class="Bound">j</a><a id="5714" class="Symbol">}(</a><a id="5716" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#5716" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="5718" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="5720" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="5724" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#5711" class="Bound">i</a><a id="5725" class="Symbol">)(</a><a id="5727" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#5727" class="Bound">B</a> <a id="5729" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="5731" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="5735" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#5713" class="Bound">j</a><a id="5736" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="5738" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="5740" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="5744" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="5745" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#5711" class="Bound">i</a> <a id="5747" href="Agda.Primitive.html#_%E2%8A%94_" class="Primitive Operator">⊔</a> <a id="5749" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#5713" class="Bound">j</a><a id="5750" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="5752" class="Keyword">where</a>
    <a id="×-Def₂._×_._,_" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82._%C3%97_._%2C_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">_,_</a> <a id="5766" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="5768" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#5716" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="5770" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="5772" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#5727" class="Bound">B</a> <a id="5774" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="5776" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#5716" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="5778" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82._%C3%97_" class="Datatype Operator">×</a> <a id="5780" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#5727" class="Bound">B</a>

        <a id="6524" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="6526" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#6497" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="6528" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_" class="Datatype Operator">≡</a> <a id="6530" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#6499" class="Bound">w</a> <a id="6532" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="6534" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#6507" class="Bound">y</a> <a id="6536" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_" class="Datatype Operator">≡</a> <a id="6538" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#6509" class="Bound">z</a> <a id="6540" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="6542" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="6543" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#6497" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="6545" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82._%C3%97_._%2C_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="6547" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#6507" class="Bound">y</a><a id="6548" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="6550" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_" class="Datatype Operator">≡</a> <a id="6552" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="6553" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#6499" class="Bound">w</a> <a id="6555" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82._%C3%97_._%2C_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="6557" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#6509" class="Bound">z</a><a id="6558" class="Symbol">)</a>
  <a id="6562" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Fun%E2%82%82.pair%3D" class="Function">pair=</a> <a id="6568" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_.refl" class="InductiveConstructor">refl</a> <a id="6573" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_.refl" class="InductiveConstructor">refl</a> <a id="6578" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="6580" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_.refl" class="InductiveConstructor">refl</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

The induction principle for the product type:

<p class="equation">
$$\mathsf{ind}_{A\times B} : \prod\limits_{C : A \times B \to \mathcal{U}}
  \left( \prod\limits_{x:A}\ \prod\limits_{y:B}\ \,C( (x,y) ) \right)
  \to \prod\limits_{x:A \times B}\ \,C(x)
$$
</p>

          <a id="7267" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="7269" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Ind%E2%82%82.ind" class="Function">ind</a> <a id="7273" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#7166" class="Bound">C</a> <a id="7275" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#7198" class="Bound">g</a> <a id="7277" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="7278" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#7243" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="7280" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82._%C3%97_._%2C_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="7282" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#7250" class="Bound">y</a><a id="7283" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="7285" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_" class="Datatype Operator">≡</a> <a id="7287" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#7198" class="Bound">g</a> <a id="7289" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#7243" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="7291" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#7250" class="Bound">y</a>
  <a id="7295" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Ind%E2%82%82.ind-%CE%B2" class="Function">ind-β</a> <a id="7301" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#7301" class="Bound">C</a> <a id="7303" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#7303" class="Bound">g</a> <a id="7305" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#7305" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="7307" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#7307" class="Bound">y</a> <a id="7309" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="7311" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_.refl" class="InductiveConstructor">refl</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

<p class="exercise">
Generalize $$\mathsf{uniq}_{A\times B}$$ to Σ-types, and do the same for
$$\Sigma$$-types, i.e. show induction and verify the definitional equality
is valid.
</p>

### Exercise 1.4

<div class="exercise">
Assuming as given only the <em>iterator</em> for natural numbers
<p class="equation">
$$\mathsf{ite} : \prod\limits_{C:\mathcal{U}} C \to (C \to C) \to \mathbb{N} \to C $$
</p>
with the defining equations
<p class="equation">
$$
\begin{align*}
\mathsf{ite}(C,c_0,c_s,0)               &\equiv c_0, \\
\mathsf{ite}(C,c_0,c_s,\mathsf{suc}(n)) &\equiv c_s(\mathsf{ite}(C,c_0,c_s,n)),
\end{align*}
$$
</p>
derive a function having the type of the recursor $$\mathsf{rec}$$.
Show that the defining equations of the recursor hold propositionally for this
function, using the induction principle for $$\mathbb{N}$$.
</div>

To solve this problem, let us define the recursor and also the induction principle
for natural numbers. (See more details about these functions in
[Induction on Natural Numbers]({% post_url 2018-02-12-induction-on-natural-numbers %})).

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="9372" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="ℕ-Def" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Def" class="Module">ℕ-Def</a> <a id="9385" class="Keyword">where</a>

Now, we define the iterator following the equations above:

Then, we now can define the recursor using this `ite` by iterating over the type
`ℕ × C` (*reloading recursion*?).

           <a id="10478" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#10351" class="Bound">n</a><a id="10479" class="Symbol">)</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

Now, we need to establish the propositional equality between these two
definitions of recursor, i.e, between `rec` and `rec₂`. Let's use
induction to prove that.

      <a id="11369" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#11305" class="Function">u</a> <a id="11371" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="11373" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Fun%E2%82%82.ap-proj%E2%82%82" class="Function">ap-proj₂</a>  <a id="11383" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="11384" class="Argument">A</a> <a id="11386" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="11388" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Def.%E2%84%95" class="Datatype">ℕ</a><a id="11389" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="11391" class="Argument">B</a> <a id="11393" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="11395" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#11008" class="Bound">C</a><a id="11396" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="11398" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="11399" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#ex1-4.proof" class="Function">proof</a> <a id="11405" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#11008" class="Bound">C</a> <a id="11407" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#11010" class="Bound">c₀</a> <a id="11410" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#11013" class="Bound">cₛ</a> <a id="11413" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#11021" class="Bound">n</a><a id="11414" class="Symbol">)</a>{% endraw %}</pre>


### Exercise 1.5

<div class="exercise">

Show that if we define

  $$A+B :\equiv \sum\limits_{(x : \mathbbbold{2})} \mathsf{rec}_{\mathbbbold{2}} (\mathcal{U}, A , B, x),$$

then we can give a definition of $$\ind\limits_{A + B}$$ for which the
definitional equalities holds.

</div>

To solve this problem, let us introduce the $$\mathcal{2}$$ type, that is, the
type with two constructors also called **Bool**. The constructors are also called
false and true respectively.

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="11919" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="𝟚-Def₁" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81" class="Module">𝟚-Def₁</a> <a id="11933" class="Keyword">where</a>

  <a id="11942" class="Keyword">data</a> <a id="𝟚-Def₁.𝟚" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81.%F0%9D%9F%9A" class="Datatype">𝟚</a> <a id="11949" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="11951" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="11955" class="Keyword">where</a>
    <a id="𝟚-Def₁.𝟚.𝟘" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81.%F0%9D%9F%9A.%F0%9D%9F%98" class="InductiveConstructor">𝟘</a> <a id="11967" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="11969" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81.%F0%9D%9F%9A" class="Datatype">𝟚</a>
    <a id="𝟚-Def₁.𝟚.𝟙" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81.%F0%9D%9F%9A.%F0%9D%9F%99" class="InductiveConstructor">𝟙</a> <a id="11977" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="11979" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81.%F0%9D%9F%9A" class="Datatype">𝟚</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

  <a id="12638" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#12638" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="12640" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%2B-Def%E2%82%81._%2B_" class="Function Operator">+</a> <a id="12642" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#12642" class="Bound">B</a> <a id="12644" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="12646" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81.%CE%A3" class="Record">Σ</a> <a id="12648" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81.%F0%9D%9F%9A" class="Datatype">𝟚</a> <a id="12650" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="12651" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Rec%E2%82%81.rec" class="Function">rec</a> <a id="12655" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#12638" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="12657" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#12642" class="Bound">B</a><a id="12658" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="12660" class="Comment">-- if it&#39;s 𝟘 return A otherwise returns B</a>

  <a id="12705" class="Comment">-- the tradional constructors</a>
  <a id="+-Def₁.inl" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%2B-Def%E2%82%81.inl" class="Function">inl</a> <a id="12741" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="12743" class="Symbol">∀</a> <a id="12745" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="12746" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#12746" class="Bound">i</a><a id="12747" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="12749" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#12749" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="12751" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#12751" class="Bound">B</a> <a id="12753" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="12755" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="12759" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#12746" class="Bound">i</a><a id="12760" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="12762" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="12764" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#12749" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="12766" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="12768" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#12749" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="12770" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%2B-Def%E2%82%81._%2B_" class="Function Operator">+</a> <a id="12772" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#12751" class="Bound">B</a>

Now, let's try to define the recursor for this coproduct, and later,
we'll try the dependent version of it to complete the exercise.

  <a id="13217" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%2B-Rec%E2%82%81.rec" class="Function">rec</a> <a id="13221" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#13221" class="Bound">f</a> <a id="13223" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#13223" class="Bound">g</a> <a id="13225" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="13226" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81.%F0%9D%9F%9A.%F0%9D%9F%99" class="InductiveConstructor">𝟙</a> <a id="13228" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81.%CE%A3._%2C_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="13230" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#13230" class="Bound">b</a><a id="13231" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="13233" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="13235" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#13223" class="Bound">g</a> <a id="13237" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#13230" class="Bound">b</a>{% endraw %}</pre>


Notice how the recursor of the coproduct matches with the elimination
rule of the disjunction conective also called *case analysis*. That's follows from the
[**propositions-as-types**](https://ncatlab.org/nlab/show/propositions+as+types).

![path](/assets/latexit-images/disj-elimination.png)

Finally, the induction principle for the coproduct:

  <a id="13675" class="Keyword">open</a> <a id="13680" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81" class="Module">𝟚-Def₁</a> <a id="13687" class="Keyword">using</a> <a id="13693" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="13694" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81.%F0%9D%9F%9A.%F0%9D%9F%98" class="InductiveConstructor">𝟘</a><a id="13695" class="Symbol">;</a><a id="13696" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81.%F0%9D%9F%9A.%F0%9D%9F%99" class="InductiveConstructor">𝟙</a><a id="13697" class="Symbol">;</a><a id="13698" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81.%F0%9D%9F%9A" class="Datatype">𝟚</a><a id="13699" class="Symbol">)</a>

## Chapter 2



## Chapter 3

To solve the following exercises, let us recall a few things:

- The *set* definition in HoTT:

A type $$A$$ is a **set** if for all $$x, y : A$$ and
all $$p, q : x \equiv y$$, we have $$ p \equiv q$$. In a proposition
we have

$$
\mathsf{isSet}(A) :\equiv \prod\limits_{(x,y : A)}\prod\limits_{(p,q : x \equiv y)} (p \equiv q).
$$

- The type for equivalence from $$A$$ to $$B$$

$$
  (A \simeq B) :\equiv \sum\limits_{f : A \to B} \mathsf{isequiv}(f),
$$

where

$$
\mathsf{isequiv(f)} :\equiv
  \left (\sum\limits_{g : B \to A} (f \circ g \sim \mathsf{id}_{B})\right) \times
  \left (\sum\limits_{h : B \to A} (h \circ f \sim \mathsf{id}_{A})\right)
$$

- The homotopy concept:

Let $$f , g : \prod\limits_{(x:A)} P(x)$$ be two sections of a
type family $$P : A \to \mathcal{U}$$. A **homotopy** from $$f$$ to $$g$$
is a dependent function of type

$$
(f \sim g) :\equiv \prod\limits_{x : A} (f(x) \equiv g(x)).
$$

### Exercise 3.1

<div class="exercise">
Prove that if $$A\simeq B$$ and $$A$$ is a set, then so is $$B$$.
</div>


<div class="proof" id="proof-3.1">
Sketch of the proof.<br/>
Let be $$x,y : B$$ and $$p : x \equiv_{B} y$$ and $$q : x \equiv_{B} y$$.
We need to prove $$ p \equiv q$$.<br/>
Since $$A\simeq B$$ then there is a function $$f : A \to B$$ and some
$$g : B \to A$$ such that $$f \circ g \sim id_{B}$$.
Using this function $$g$$ over the path $$p$$ we get
$$\mathsf{ap}_{g} p : g x \equiv_{A} g y$$.
We do the same but this time over the path $$q$$, that is,
$$\mathsf{ap}_{g} q : g x \equiv_{A} g y$$.
Because of $$A$$ is a set, we have a new path called
$$m :\mathsf{ap}_{g} p \equiv_{gx \equiv_{A} gy} \mathsf{ap}_{g} q$$. <br/>

Now, an action over this path $$m$$
using the function $$\mathsf{ap}_{f} : x \equiv_{A} y \to f x \equiv_{B} f y$$
will give us

<p class="equation">
$$
\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{ap}_{f}} m :
(\mathsf{ap}_{f}) (\mathsf{ap}_{g} p) \equiv (\mathsf{ap}_{f})  (\mathsf{ap}_{g} q).
$$
</p>
By the lemmas in Chapter 2, we do the following reasoning:

<p class="equation">
$$
\begin{align*}
(\mathsf{ap}_{f}) (\mathsf{ap}_{g} p) \equiv (\mathsf{ap}_{f})  (\mathsf{ap}_{g} q) &=
  \mathsf{ap}_{f \circ g} p \equiv \mathsf{ap}_{f \circ g} q\\
  &=\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{id}_{B}} p \equiv \mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{id}_{B}} q\\
  &= p \equiv q.
\end{align*}
$$<br/>
</p>
Then, we have the inhabitant, $$\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{ap}_{f}} m : p \equiv q$$.
</div>

Now, let's verify this in Agda.

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="16804" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="sets" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#sets" class="Module">sets</a> <a id="16816" class="Keyword">where</a>

  <a id="16861" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#sets.isSet" class="Function">isSet</a> <a id="16867" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% class="Bound">x</a> <a id="16874" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#16874" class="Bound">y</a> <a id="16876" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="16878" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-HoTT-book.md %}{% raw %}#16867" class="Bound">A</a><a id="16879" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="16881" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="16883" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="16884" href="{% ### Exercise 3.2

<div class="exercise">
Prove that if $$A$$ and $$B$$ are sets, then so is $$A+B$$.
</div>

To solve this exercise, we should take a look of some results from Chapter 2,
Section 2.12.

<div class="proof" id="proof-3.2">
Sketch of the Proof.<br/>

Let be $$x, y : A + B$$, and paths $$p : x \equiv y$$, $$q : x \equiv
y$$. Let's get a path $$p \equiv q$$.  We proceed by case analysis. If
$$x :\equiv \mathsf{inl} a$$ and $$y :\equiv \mathsf{inl} b$$, for
some $$a, b : A$$ then $$\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}^{-1}} p : a
\equiv_{A} b$$ and $$\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}^{-1}} q : a \equiv_{A}
b$$.

Since $$A$$ is a set, there is a path between these last two terms,
this is, $$m : \mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}^{-1}} p \equiv
\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}^{-1}} q$$.  Now, an action over this path
$$m$$ using the $$\mathsf{inl}$$ function give us:
$$\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}} m : \mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}}
(\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}^{-1}} p) \equiv \mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}}
(\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}^{-1}} q)$$.<br/>

We conclude by Lemmas in Chapter 2, that $$\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}}
m : p \equiv q$$ since $$\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}}
(\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}^{-1}} p) \equiv p$$.<br/> Following the
same reasoning, we prove the case $$x :\equiv \mathsf{inr} a$$ and $$y
:\equiv \mathsf{inr} b$$.  For the latest cases, $$x :\equiv
\mathsf{inl} a$$ and $$y :\equiv \mathsf{inr} b$$ and $$x :\equiv
\mathsf{inr} a$$ and $$y :\equiv \mathsf{inl} b$$, we use the
encode-decode method to derive a proof term for 𝟘 from
$$p$$ and $$q$$. Then, we may conclude anything we wish, that is, $$p
\equiv q$$.
</div>

But first let's define the empty type:

  <a id="19287" class="Comment">-- ind : {A B : Set}</a>
  <a id="19310" class="Comment">--     → (C : A + B → Set)</a>
  <a id="19339" class="Comment">--     → ((x : A) → C (inl x))</a>
  <a id="19372" class="Comment">--     → ((x : B) → C (inr x))</a>
  <a id="19405" class="Comment">--     → (x : A + B) → C x</a>
  <a id="19434" class="Comment">-- ind C f g c x = {!   !}</a>

### Exercise 3.3

<div class="exercise">
Prove that if $$ A $$ is a set and $$B : A \to \mathcal{U}$$
is a type family such that $$B(x)$$ is a set for all
$$x : A$$, then $$\Sigma\limits_{(x:A)}\ B(x)$$ is a set.
</div>

### Exercise 3.4

<div class="exercise">
Show that $$A$$ is a mere proposition if and only
if $$A\to A$$ is contractible.
</div>

* Univalent Foundations Program, T. (2013). Homotopy Type Theory: Univalent Foundations of Mathematics. Institute for Advanced Study.

* [Capriotti's hott-exercises](https://github.com/pcapriotti/hott-exercises).

* [Capriotti's agda-base](https://github.com/pcapriotti/agda-base/)
